<p>One reason given for the increase in <i>The Daily Show</i> and <i>Colbert Report</i> ratings was the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2008" title="United States presidential election, 2008">2008 presidential election</a>, allowing them a large amount of political humor to use. However, one journalist commented that the raise of ratings in these two shows without the writers, "has to be a big PR setback for the WGA."<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the strike began, more unscripted shows were ordered by networks, most coming from the reality genre.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Entertainment_award_telecasts">Entertainment award telecasts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_Writers_Guild_of_America_strike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Entertainment award telecasts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The writers' strike also created turmoil for various entertainment awards that were broadcast on television. Many awards were severely curtailed or canceled as a result.</p>
<p>As a result of the <a href="/wiki/Screen_Actors_Guild" title="Screen Actors Guild">Screen Actors Guild</a>'s solidarity with the WGA, they gave the SAG a waiver on December 11 granting permission for guild writers to create material for the <a href="/wiki/14th_Screen_Actors_Guild_Awards" title="14th Screen Actors Guild Awards">14th Screen Actors Guild Awards</a> which was shown on <a href="/wiki/Turner_Network_Television" class="mw-redirect" title="Turner Network Television">TNT</a> and <a href="/wiki/TBS_(TV_network)" class="mw-redirect" title="TBS (TV network)">TBS</a> on January 27.<sup id="cite_ref-tbs_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tbs-129">[129]</a></sup> The WGA also issued one nine days later allowing writers to write material for <a href="/wiki/Independent_Spirit_Awards" title="Independent Spirit Awards">Film Independent's Spirit Awards</a> on February 23.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup></p>
<p>On December 18, the WGA announced it would not issue waivers for the <a href="/wiki/65th_Golden_Globe_Awards" title="65th Golden Globe Awards">Golden Globe Awards</a> and <a href="/wiki/80th_Academy_Awards" title="80th Academy Awards">Academy Awards</a> (Oscars) ceremonies. In an act of solidarity, SAG also decided not to support the Golden Globes as well.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> Labor experts stated that this move was "an attempt by the guild to bring the Alliance of Motion Picture and Television Producers back to the bargaining table."<sup id="cite_ref-apindie_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-apindie-133">[133]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Choice_Awards" title="People's Choice Awards">People's Choice Awards</a>, which was also denied a waiver, stated it would have to revamp the format of the ceremony by releasing a taped ceremony for January 8 telecast on CBS, instead of airing it live as usual.<sup id="cite_ref-apindie_133-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-apindie-133">[133]</a></sup> As a result of the changes which were made, the telecast was viewed by just 6 million viewers, the lowest ratings ever in the show's history.<sup id="cite_ref-pcalowratings_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pcalowratings-134">[134]</a></sup> This was down from 11.3 million viewers the previous year.<sup id="cite_ref-pcalowratings_134-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pcalowratings-134">[134]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pcaratings2007_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pcaratings2007-135">[135]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pcalowratings2_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pcalowratings2-136">[136]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Foreign_Press_Association" title="Hollywood Foreign Press Association">Hollywood Foreign Press Association</a> (HFPA), which hosts the Golden Globes, tried to reach an agreement with the WGA for a waiver, but it fell through. Striking writers then threatened to picket the event, after which almost all of the celebrities due to attend announced they would skip the ceremony rather than cross the picket lines. Facing the prospect of being left without presenters or accepters, HFPA and NBC were forced to adopt another approach for the broadcast. After NBC canceled its exclusive newscast of HFPA announcing the winners, HFPA took complete control of the awards announcement and opened its press conference to all media. WGA assured HFPA that it would not picket the event, citing HFPA's honesty and its honorable and respectful treatment of the guild as reasons.<sup id="cite_ref-ggformat_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ggformat-137">[137]</a></sup> The NBC telecast plummeted in the ratings from 16.0 for the full ceremony in 2007 to 4.7 for the press conference in 2008, fourth (and last) among major networks that night.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup></p>
<p>The WGA issued two more waivers for awards telecast. One was issued towards the <a href="/wiki/NAACP" class="mw-redirect" title="NAACP">NAACP</a> on January 15 for the <a href="/wiki/NAACP_Image_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="NAACP Image Awards">NAACP Image Awards</a> a month later,<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> and one on January 29 to the <a href="/wiki/NARAS" class="mw-redirect" title="NARAS">NARAS</a> for the <a href="/wiki/50th_Grammy_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="50th Grammy Awards">50th Grammy Awards</a> held on February 10.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup></p>
<p>The strike ended twelve days before the Academy Awards were held on February 24. Many blamed the strike for the show's low television ratings, since the writers had less time to prepare. The strike also hindered promotion at ABC, the broadcaster in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Television_viewership">Television viewership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_Writers_Guild_of_America_strike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Television viewership">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A white paper released by <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_Media_Research" title="Nielsen Media Research">Nielsen Media Research</a> on April 2, 2008 showed that most television viewers spent more time around alternative forms of entertainment outside of broadcast television, including cable television and online video sites, during the course of the strike.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> Compared with the same time period from 2006–2007, during the months of the strike (November 2007 through February 2008) the average primetime ratings for that time period declined by 6.8%.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Response">Response</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_Writers_Guild_of_America_strike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Response">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Actors">Actors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_Writers_Guild_of_America_strike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Actors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:25%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>They claim there’s no money in the Internet. That’s a <a href="/wiki/Shell_game" title="Shell game">shell game</a>.</p>
</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: left;">--Actor <a href="/wiki/Robin_Williams" title="Robin Williams">Robin Williams</a><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup></cite></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Screen_Actors_Guild" title="Screen Actors Guild">Screen Actors Guild</a> and <a href="/wiki/American_Federation_of_Television_and_Radio_Artists" title="American Federation of Television and Radio Artists">American Federation of Television and Radio Artists</a> (AFTRA) contracts with the <a href="/wiki/Alliance_of_Motion_Picture_and_Television_Producers" title="Alliance of Motion Picture and Television Producers">AMPTP</a> both contain a "no strike" clause, meaning that working members of the acting unions are not supposed to walk off their set in support of another union's strike. However, many actors, backed by their unions, expressed their support and solidarity with the writers' strike, with some marching with writers and even refusing to cross the WGA's picket line.<sup id="cite_ref-SAGAlan_127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SAGAlan-127">[127]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-picketwithstars_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-picketwithstars-145">[145]</a></sup> Many actors participated in a series of short PSAs as part of the Speechless Without Writers<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> campaign presented by United Hollywood,<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> which was founded by a group of WGA members.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="List_of_actors_picketing">List of actors picketing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_Writers_Guild_of_America_strike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: List of actors picketing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="div-col columns column-count column-count-2" style="-moz-column-count: 2; -webkit-column-count: 2; column-count: 2;">
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Amy_Acker" title="Amy Acker">Amy Acker</a><sup id="cite_ref-whedonesque14886_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whedonesque14886-149">[149]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alan_Tudyk" title="Alan Tudyk">Alan Tudyk</a><sup id="cite_ref-whedonesque14922_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whedonesque14922-150">[150]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alex_Kapp_Horner" title="Alex Kapp Horner">Alex Kapp Horner</a><sup id="cite_ref-picketwithstars_145-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-picketwithstars-145">[145]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ali_Larter" title="Ali Larter">Ali Larter</a><sup id="cite_ref-heroes-strike_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heroes-strike-151">[151]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alyson_Hannigan" title="Alyson Hannigan">Alyson Hannigan</a><sup id="cite_ref-picketatuniversal_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-picketatuniversal-152">[152]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/America_Ferrera" title="America Ferrera">America Ferrera</a><sup id="cite_ref-ferrera_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ferrera-153">[153]</a></sup></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Joaquin_Phoenix" title="Joaquin Phoenix">Joaquin Phoenix</a><sup id="cite_ref-Contactmusic.com_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Contactmusic.com-214">[214]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jon_Stewart" title="Jon Stewart">Jon Stewart</a><sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Justine_Bateman" title="Justine Bateman">Justine Bateman</a><sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kristen_Bell" title="Kristen Bell">Kristen Bell</a><sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ray_Bradbury" title="Ray Bradbury">Ray Bradbury</a><sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Reese_Witherspoon" title="Reese Witherspoon">Reese Witherspoon</a><sup id="cite_ref-Contactmusic.com_214-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Contactmusic.com-214">[214]</a></sup></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Stephen_Colbert" title="Stephen Colbert">Stephen Colbert</a><sup id="cite_ref-TCROS_219-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TCROS-219">[219]</a></sup></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Tom_Hanks" title="Tom Hanks">Tom Hanks</a><sup id="cite_ref-hanks_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hanks-220">[220]</a></sup></li>

</ul>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ray_Bradbury_with_WGA_strike_members_at_Fox_Studios_Jan._7,_2008.pdf" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Ray_Bradbury_with_WGA_strike_members_at_Fox_Studios_Jan._7%2C_2008.pdf/page1-220px-Ray_Bradbury_with_WGA_strike_members_at_Fox_Studios_Jan._7%2C_2008.pdf.jpg" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Ray_Bradbury_with_WGA_strike_members_at_Fox_Studios_Jan._7%2C_2008.pdf/page1-330px-Ray_Bradbury_with_WGA_strike_members_at_Fox_Studios_Jan._7%2C_2008.pdf.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Ray_Bradbury_with_WGA_strike_members_at_Fox_Studios_Jan._7%2C_2008.pdf/page1-440px-Ray_Bradbury_with_WGA_strike_members_at_Fox_Studios_Jan._7%2C_2008.pdf.jpg 2x" data-file-width="895" data-file-height="583" /></a>

Flam (r)).</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Talk_show_hosts">Talk show hosts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_Writers_Guild_of_America_strike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Talk show hosts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ellen_DeGeneres" title="Ellen DeGeneres">Ellen DeGeneres</a> stated she supports the strike, but crossed the picket line, though she decided not to do a monologue on her show during the strike, explaining that she did not wish to lay off the 135 employees from her staff.<sup id="cite_ref-Television:_Tears.2C_strike_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Television:_Tears.2C_strike-224">[224]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">[225]</a></sup> The WGAE issued a statement condemning DeGeneres, stating she was "not welcome in NY."<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">[226]</a></sup> DeGeneres' representatives asserted that she did not violate the WGA's agreement, arguing that she is competing with other first-run syndicated shows like <i><a href="/wiki/Dr._Phil" class="mw-redirect" title="Dr. Phil">Dr. Phil</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Regis_and_Kelly" class="mw-redirect" title="Regis and Kelly">Regis and Kelly</a></i> during the competitive November <a href="/wiki/Sweeps" class="mw-redirect" title="Sweeps">sweeps</a> period, and that DeGeneres must fulfill her duties as host and producers, lest her show lose its time slot or be held in breach of contract. In addition, a statement defending DeGeneres was subsequently issued by <a href="/wiki/American_Federation_of_Television_and_Radio_Artists" title="American Federation of Television and Radio Artists">American Federation of Television and Radio Artists</a> (AFTRA), pointing out that DeGeneres also works under the AFTRA TV Code, which bars her from striking. The <a href="/wiki/WGAE" class="mw-redirect" title="WGAE">WGAE</a> then issued a response pointing out that DeGeneres is also a Writers Guild member, and that any writing work she does on her show during the strike constitutes struck work.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">[227]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">[228]</a></sup></p>
<p>Early in the strike, it was rumored that <a href="/wiki/Jon_Stewart" title="Jon Stewart">Jon Stewart</a> was continuing to pay his <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Show" title="The Daily Show">Daily Show</a></i> writers out of his own pocket, but a spokesman later denied the rumor was true.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">[229]</a></sup> However, <i>The Daily Show</i> temporarily changed its name to <i><b>A</b> Daily Show</i> to show its support of the strike. <a href="/wiki/Nikki_Finke" title="Nikki Finke">Nikki Finke</a> announced that <a href="/wiki/David_Letterman" title="David Letterman">David Letterman</a> would pay his entire staff's salary out of his own pocket through the end of the year.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">[230]</a></sup> She later announced that following NBC's firing of eighty staffers on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tonight_Show" title="The Tonight Show">The Tonight Show</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Jay_Leno" title="Jay Leno">Jay Leno</a> would continue paying them out of his own pocket as well.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">[231]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Conan_O%27Brien" title="Conan O'Brien">Conan O'Brien</a> also promised to pay the salaries of his non-striking staff through the end of the year.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">[232]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some comedy shows have performed live shows in order to provide money for the striking workers in a series of <i>ON STRIKE!</i> performances at the <a href="/wiki/Upright_Citizens_Brigade_Theater" class="mw-redirect" title="Upright Citizens Brigade Theater">Upright Citizens Brigade Theater</a>. The first two shows to perform were <i><a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live" title="Saturday Night Live">Saturday Night Live</a></i> on November 17, and <i><a href="/wiki/30_Rock" title="30 Rock">30 Rock</a></i> on November 19.<sup id="cite_ref-SNL_.26_30R_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SNL_.26_30R-233">[233]</a></sup> On December 3, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Colbert_Report" title="The Colbert Report">The Colbert Report</a></i> held a similar performance.<sup id="cite_ref-TCROS_219-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TCROS-219">[219]</a></sup></p>
<p>Host <a href="/wiki/Bill_Maher" title="Bill Maher">Bill Maher</a> vocally criticized the movement as the wrong time to carry out such a strike.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Writer-producers">Writer-producers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_Writers_Guild_of_America_strike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Writer-producers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Seth_mcfarlane_speaks_at_wga_rally.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Seth_mcfarlane_speaks_at_wga_rally.jpg/220px-Seth_mcfarlane_speaks_at_wga_rally.jpg" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Seth_mcfarlane_speaks_at_wga_rally.jpg/330px-Seth_mcfarlane_speaks_at_wga_rally.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Seth_mcfarlane_speaks_at_wga_rally.jpg/440px-Seth_mcfarlane_speaks_at_wga_rally.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="719" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Seth_mcfarlane_speaks_at_wga_rally.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i><a href="/wiki/Family_Guy" title="Family Guy">Family Guy</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/American_Dad!" title="American Dad!">American Dad!</a></i> creator and actor <a href="/wiki/Seth_MacFarlane" title="Seth MacFarlane">Seth MacFarlane</a> speaks at a WGAW rally in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a> on November 9, 2007.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Many television writer-producers, also known as "<a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/hyphenate" class="extiw" title="wikt:hyphenate">hyphenates</a>" (or "<a href="/wiki/Show_runner" class="mw-redirect" title="Show runner">show-runners</a>", if they are in charge of the day-to-day production of a television show) who are WGA members found themselves contractually obligated to continue their production duties while simultaneously barred from performing writing duties during the strike. In a show of solidarity with the writers, approximately 120 show-runners marched in Burbank on November 7, 2007, and many decided to honor the picket lines entirely, refusing to perform even their production duties during the strike.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">[234]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agents">Agents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_Writers_Guild_of_America_strike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Agents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Literary_agents" class="mw-redirect" title="Literary agents">Literary agents</a> stand to lose business when the writers they represent are not working. Some agencies reportedly eliminated assistant positions and others asked their agents to take pay cuts during the strike.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup> A few of the larger and more prominent agencies, including <a href="/wiki/William_Morris_Agency" title="William Morris Agency">William Morris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Creative_Artists_Agency" title="Creative Artists Agency">CAA</a>, and <a href="/wiki/International_Creative_Management" class="mw-redirect" title="International Creative Management">ICM</a> provided <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">coffee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bagel" title="Bagel">bagels</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Churro" title="Churro">churros</a> for picketing writers.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">[236]</a></sup> Agents had also reportedly been involved in <a href="/wiki/Chain_of_command" class="mw-redirect" title="Chain of command">back-channel</a> efforts to get the two parties to return to the negotiating table before talks resumed November 26.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">[237]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_executives">Media executives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_Writers_Guild_of_America_strike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Media executives">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Two prominent executives, both of whom headed major studios in the 1980s and moved on to Internet-related ventures, voiced their disagreement with the tactics of the WGA.</p>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:33%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>For a writer to give up today's money for a nonexistent piece of the future — they should do it in three years, shouldn't be doing it now — they are misguided; they should not have gone on the strike.</p>
</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: left;">Michael Eisner, new-media executive<sup id="cite_ref-eisner_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eisner-238">[238]</a></sup></cite></div>
<p>Former <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Walt Disney Corporation">Walt Disney Corporation</a> CEO <a href="/wiki/Michael_Eisner" title="Michael Eisner">Michael Eisner</a> characterized the writers' strike as "insanity". He addressed a business conference, saying, "I've seen stupid strikes, I've seen less stupid strikes, and this strike is just a stupid strike".<sup id="cite_ref-eisner_238-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eisner-238">[238]</a></sup></p>
<p>Former Paramount and Fox CEO <a href="/wiki/Barry_Diller" title="Barry Diller">Barry Diller</a> also stated the strike is "stupid". In comments to <a href="/wiki/Fox_Business_Channel" class="mw-redirect" title="Fox Business Channel">Fox Business Channel</a>, he said, "There are no profits for the work that writers do that is then digitized and distributed through the Internet". Diller is currently the CEO of the Internet conglomerate <a href="/wiki/IAC/InterActiveCorp" class="mw-redirect" title="IAC/InterActiveCorp">IAC/InterActiveCorp</a>.</p>
<p>Diller also suggested that the Writers Guild should have waited five years to see where the revenues from new-media ventures were coming from. "We want to freeze this area until we can understand the revenues, which aren’t going to develop for another few years".<sup id="cite_ref-diller_239-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diller-239">[239]</a></sup></p>
<p>Neither executive, however, expressed support for the AMPTP.<sup id="cite_ref-eisner_238-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eisner-238">[238]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-diller_239-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diller-239">[239]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:John_Edwards_WGA_strike.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/John_Edwards_WGA_strike.jpg/220px-John_Edwards_WGA_strike.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/John_Edwards_WGA_strike.jpg/330px-John_Edwards_WGA_strike.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/John_Edwards_WGA_strike.jpg/440px-John_Edwards_WGA_strike.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="1880" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:John_Edwards_WGA_strike.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Former presidential candidate John Edwards attends November 16, 2007, rally for striking writers at a WGAW protest at <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a> in <a href="/wiki/Burbank,_California" title="Burbank, California">Burbank</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Politicians">Politicians</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_Writers_Guild_of_America_strike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Politicians">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a> governor at the time, <a href="/wiki/Arnold_Schwarzenegger" title="Arnold Schwarzenegger">Arnold Schwarzenegger</a>, negotiated with both sides of the dispute "because it has a tremendous economic impact on our state."<sup id="cite_ref-cbc_schwarz_240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbc_schwarz-240">[240]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/2008_Democratic_presidential_candidates" class="mw-redirect" title="2008 Democratic presidential candidates">2008 Democratic presidential candidates</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senator" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Senator">Senator</a> and eventual <a href="/wiki/United_States_President" class="mw-redirect" title="United States President">President</a> <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>, Sen. <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a>, Sen. <a href="/wiki/John_Edwards" title="John Edwards">John Edwards</a>, and Gov. <a href="/wiki/Bill_Richardson" title="Bill Richardson">Bill Richardson</a>, each issued statements of support for the WGA.<sup id="cite_ref-presidents_241-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-presidents-241">[241]</a></sup> Although <a href="/wiki/2008_Republican_presidential_candidates" class="mw-redirect" title="2008 Republican presidential candidates">2008 Republican presidential candidate</a> <a href="/wiki/Rudy_Giuliani" title="Rudy Giuliani">Rudy Giuliani</a> stated that "a candidate for office really shouldn't get involved," he did offer to serve as a mediator between the parties, citing his experience "settl[ing] several difficult labor disputes" as Mayor of <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">[242]</a></sup> Civil rights leader and former presidential candidate <a href="/wiki/Jesse_Jackson" title="Jesse Jackson">Jesse Jackson</a> marched with the writers and spoke at a WGA rally on November 9, 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">[243]</a></sup> On November 13, 2007, the Los Angeles County Democratic Party adopted a resolution in support of the WGA.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">[244]</a></sup> WGAW president <a href="/wiki/Patric_Verrone" title="Patric Verrone">Patric Verrone</a> and <a href="/wiki/Screen_Actors_Guild" title="Screen Actors Guild">Screen Actors Guild</a> president <a href="/wiki/Alan_Rosenberg" title="Alan Rosenberg">Alan Rosenberg</a> traveled to <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a> on November 14 to meet with legislators and regulators about the unions' position on new media.<sup id="cite_ref-variety-dc_245-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-variety-dc-245">[245]</a></sup> On November 16, <a href="/wiki/John_Edwards" title="John Edwards">John Edwards</a> appeared in person to picket and speak with the writers outside NBC studios in Burbank, CA.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">[246]</a></sup> The December 10, 2007, Democratic Presidential debate that was to be held in Los Angeles, California, was cancelled on November 28, 2007, due to candidate boycott.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">[247]</a></sup></p>
<p>On December 19, 2007, <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_City_Council" title="Los Angeles City Council">Los Angeles City Council</a>’s Housing, Community, and Economic Development Committee held a hearing on the economic impact of the strike on the local and regional economy, allowing the WGA and AMPTP to testify. However, the AMPTP declined to attend, but sent in <a href="/wiki/Motion_Picture_Association_of_America" title="Motion Picture Association of America">Motion Picture Association of America</a> to issue a statement to the committee on its behalf. The Los Angeles City Council approved a resolution which urged the two sides to return to the bargaining table.<sup id="cite_ref-citycouncil_248-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-citycouncil-248">[248]</a></sup> Jerry Nickelsburg, an economics professor at <a href="/wiki/UCLA_Anderson_School_of_Management" title="UCLA Anderson School of Management">UCLA Anderson School of Management</a>, presented UCLA Anderson Forecast's economic report. He stated that so far, the strike has not affected the economy deeply, citing the network's inventory stockpiling in preparation of the strike and the increase in usage of reality shows.<sup id="cite_ref-econforecast_249-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-econforecast-249">[249]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-uclaforecast_250-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uclaforecast-250">[250]</a></sup> Ultimately, the Forecast predicted an economic impact of $380 million if the strike were to last 22 weeks, which was how long the 1988 strike had lasted.<sup id="cite_ref-econforecast_249-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-econforecast-249">[249]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-uclaforecast_250-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uclaforecast-250">[250]</a></sup> Jack Kyser, an economist of Los Angeles County Economic Development Corporation, predicted that the total amount of the direct loss and indirect loss so far was estimated at $220 million, and revenues generated for the county from the annual Academy Awards would dip if the strike were to continue and actors honored the picket lines.<sup id="cite_ref-econforecast_249-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-econforecast-249">[249]</a></sup> The strike ended twelve days before the awards show.</p>
<p>On January 3, 2008, Republican presidential candidate <a href="/wiki/Mike_Huckabee" title="Mike Huckabee">Mike Huckabee</a> appeared on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tonight_Show" title="The Tonight Show">The Tonight Show</a></i>. "I support the writers, by the way. Unequivocally, absolutely. They're dead right on this one... I don't think anybody supports the producers on this one. Maybe the producers support the producers, but I think everybody in the business and even the general public supports the writers."<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">[251]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_unions_and_associations">Other unions and associations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_Writers_Guild_of_America_strike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Other unions and associations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The WGA acknowledged support from several unions, including the <a href="/wiki/Screen_Actors_Guild" title="Screen Actors Guild">Screen Actors Guild</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Teamsters" class="mw-redirect" title="Teamsters">Teamsters</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Service_Employees_International_Union" title="Service Employees International Union">Service Employees International Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/International_Longshore_and_Warehouse_Union" title="International Longshore and Warehouse Union">International Longshore and Warehouse Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/National_Writers_Union" title="National Writers Union">National Writers Union</a>, as well as writers guilds in Canada, Australia, Great Britain, Germany, New Zealand, France, Netherlands, Greece, Ireland, Switzerland, and Belgium.<sup id="cite_ref-dvd_proposal_removal_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dvd_proposal_removal-23">[23]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">[252]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-dayofsupport_253-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dayofsupport-253">[253]</a></sup> Many of the various genre writers associations also came out in support of the WGA's strike, including the <a href="/wiki/Horror_Writers_Association" title="Horror Writers Association">Horror Writers Association</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-horror_254-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-horror-254">[254]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Mystery_Writers_of_America" title="Mystery Writers of America">Mystery Writers of America</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-mysteryg_255-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mysteryg-255">[255]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Science_Fiction_and_Fantasy_Writers_of_America" title="Science Fiction and Fantasy Writers of America">Science Fiction and Fantasy Writers of America</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">[256]</a></sup></p>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:33%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>The numbers speak for themselves and show that the WGA leadership is totally out of touch with the impact of their foolhardy tactics. Figures don't lie, liars figure.</p>
</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: left;">IATSE president Tom Short<sup id="cite_ref-IATSE_257-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IATSE-257">[257]</a></sup></cite></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/International_Alliance_of_Theatrical_Stage_Employees" title="International Alliance of Theatrical Stage Employees">International Alliance of Theatrical Stage Employees</a>, which represents most of the <a href="/wiki/Below_the_line_(film_production)" class="mw-redirect" title="Below the line (film production)">below-the-line</a> motion picture employees (over 50,000 members) and has jurisdictional disputes with WGAW in animation,<sup id="cite_ref-bitchslapping_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bitchslapping-45">[45]</a></sup> did not join the strike, citing a "no strike" provision in their contracts.<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">[258]</a></sup> IATSE president Tom Short has publicly criticized the tactics of the WGA, arguing that the Writers Guild intended to strike almost a year in advance of the expiration of the writers' contract. In a letter to Verrone made publicly available, Short wrote, "When I phoned you on Nov. 28, 2006, to ask you to reconsider the timing of negotiations, you refused. It now seems that you were intending that there be a strike no matter what you were offered, or what conditions the industry faced when your contract expired at the end of October."<sup id="cite_ref-bitchslapping_45-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bitchslapping-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="General_public">General public</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_Writers_Guild_of_America_strike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: General public">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Several opinion polls gauged the public's response to the strike. One national survey conducted by <a href="/wiki/Pepperdine_University" title="Pepperdine University">Pepperdine University</a> from November 7 to November 9 found that 84%, or more than four out of five Americans, were aware the strike was in progress.<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">[259]</a></sup> While 75% of respondents were found to have little to no concern over the strike, nearly two-thirds of the sample sided with the writers, one third was unsure, and only four percent sympathized with the AMPTP (1,000 American adults participated). A second regional poll conducted by <a href="/wiki/SurveyUSA" title="SurveyUSA">SurveyUSA</a> on November 11 of Los Angeles residents indicated that eight percent supported the studios with sixty-nine percent supporting the writers (550 American adults participated, with 482 identifying themselves as being familiar with the strike).<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">[260]</a></sup> According to a USA Today/Gallup Poll conducted six weeks into the strike from December 13 to December 15, 60% of Americans side with the writers, while 14% favor the studios (1,011 American adults participated). Among the viewers, 49% said they were more likely to watch reruns, 40% said they planned to watch reality series and other programming not disrupted by the strike, and 26% were more likely to buy or rent DVDs of television series from past seasons.<sup id="cite_ref-usagalluppoll_261-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usagalluppoll-261">[261]</a></sup> Viewers of late-night talk shows have already changed their habits: out of 25% of the poll respondents who said they frequently or occasionally watch late-night talk shows, 27% watched another show, 25% went to bed earlier, and 25% read. Only 12% watched reruns, indicated by the shows' decreasing ratings.<sup id="cite_ref-usagalluppoll_261-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usagalluppoll-261">[261]</a></sup></p>
<p>Viewers of individual television shows organized to support "their" writers. <a href="/wiki/Fans4Writers" title="Fans4Writers">Fans4Writers</a>, an outgrowth of <a href="/wiki/Joss_Whedon" title="Joss Whedon">Joss Whedon</a>'s fan base, walked the picket line and provided regular food drops to picketing writers.<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">[262]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">[263]</a></sup> Additionally, one of the largest fan-based pickets began the morning of January 24, 2008, at NBC Studios in Burbank when fans of the series <a href="/wiki/Xena:_Warrior_Princess" title="Xena: Warrior Princess">Xena: Warrior Princess</a>, a popular series which had ceased production in 2001, lined up to march in support of the WGA. Producers and actors from the TV show joined the line, including performers <a href="/wiki/Renee_O%27Connor" title="Renee O'Connor">Renee O'Connor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adrienne_Wilkinson" title="Adrienne Wilkinson">Adrienne Wilkinson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tim_Omundson" class="mw-redirect" title="Tim Omundson">Tim Omundson</a> and producers <a href="/wiki/Robert_Tapert" title="Robert Tapert">Robert Tapert</a>, RJ Stewart, <a href="/wiki/Steven_L._Sears" title="Steven L. Sears">Steven L. Sears</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liz_Friedman" title="Liz Friedman">Liz Friedman</a>, and others. As with Fans4Writers, Xena fans had been donating food and water to the picket lines for the duration of the strike and an upcoming Xena Convention in Burbank offered the opportunity of a focused show of support from fans worldwide. <sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">[264]</a></sup></p>
<p>The long-term effect on the viewing habits of the general public is difficult to gauge. For reference, estimates suggest that 10% of the overall television-viewing audience was lost as a result of the 1988 writers' strike, a drop-off that has not been reversed.<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">[265]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Related_work_stoppages">Related work stoppages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_Writers_Guild_of_America_strike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Related work stoppages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Past_Hollywood_guild_walk-outs">Past Hollywood guild walk-outs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_Writers_Guild_of_America_strike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Past Hollywood guild walk-outs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Hollywood_strikes" title="List of Hollywood strikes">List of Hollywood strikes</a></div>
<div class="div-col columns column-count column-count-2" style="-moz-column-count: 2; -webkit-column-count: 2; column-count: 2;">
<ul>
<li>2000 Commercial actors strike, almost six months.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/1988_Writers_Guild_of_America_strike" title="1988 Writers Guild of America strike">1988 Writers Guild of America strike</a>, 22 weeks.</li>
<li>1987 Director's strike, 3 hours and 5&#160;minutes.</li>
<li>1985 Writers strike, two weeks.</li>
<li>1981 Writers Guild of America strike, three months.</li>
<li>1980 Actors strike, three months.</li>
<li>1960 Actors strike, led by SAG President <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a>, six weeks.</li>
<li>1952 Actors strike, two and a half months.</li>
<li>1945 Set decorators <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Black_Friday" title="Hollywood Black Friday">Hollywood Black Friday</a> strike, six months.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/1942%E2%80%9344_musicians%27_strike" title="1942–44 musicians' strike">1942–44 Musicians' strike</a>, thirteen months plus.</li>
<li>1941 <a href="/wiki/Disney_animators%27_strike" title="Disney animators' strike">Disney animators' strike</a>, five weeks.</li>
</ul>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2007.E2.80.932008_CBS_News_writers_strike">2007–2008 CBS News writers strike</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_Writers_Guild_of_America_strike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: 2007–2008 CBS News writers strike">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%932008_CBS_News_writers_strike" class="mw-redirect" title="2007–2008 CBS News writers strike">2007–2008 CBS News writers strike</a></div>
<p>On November 19, 2007, news writers for CBS News and CBS-owned stations voted to authorize strike action against their employers. Timed closely to the WGA strike, this action has resulted in statements from politicians unwilling to cross picket lines for interview shows and candidate debates. On January 9, the WGAE and CBS News struck a tentative deal.<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">[266]</a></sup> On January 24, 2008, the WGA announced that its members had voted to ratify the contract, which runs to April 1, 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">[267]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_2008_industry-wide_strike_threats">Other 2008 industry-wide strike threats</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_Writers_Guild_of_America_strike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Other 2008 industry-wide strike threats">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Any increase for the benefits of <a href="/wiki/Health_insurance" title="Health insurance">health insurance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pension" title="Pension">pension</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Residual_(entertainment_industry)" title="Residual (entertainment industry)">residual</a> gains made by the WGA are also likely to be demanded by other entertainment industry labor unions when their contracts expire. This is a practice known as <a href="/wiki/Pattern_bargaining" title="Pattern bargaining">pattern bargaining</a> — the first union to reach a contract with the AMPTP usually sets the template for the agreement with other unions. The contracts for the <a href="/wiki/Screen_Actors_Guild" title="Screen Actors Guild">Screen Actors Guild</a> (SAG) and <a href="/wiki/Directors_Guild_of_America" title="Directors Guild of America">Directors Guild of America</a> (DGA) expired on June 30, 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">[268]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Directors_Guild_of_America">Directors Guild of America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_Writers_Guild_of_America_strike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Directors Guild of America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Directors_Guild_of_America" title="Directors Guild of America">Directors Guild of America</a> (DGA), whose members are directors as well as <a href="/wiki/Below_the_line_(film_production)" class="mw-redirect" title="Below the line (film production)">below-the-line</a> workers (1st and 2nd <a href="/wiki/Assistant_director" title="Assistant director">assistant directors</a>), was less focused on the WGA's most contentious issue, <a href="/wiki/New_media" title="New media">new media</a> residuals. The DGA's negotiations with the AMPTP started on January 12, 2008, and on January 17, the DGA announced they had reached a tentative agreement.<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">[269]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DGAneg_270-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DGAneg-270">[270]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following the DGA announcement, <i><a href="/wiki/ER_(TV_series)" title="ER (TV series)">ER</a></i> executive producer and former WGA president <a href="/wiki/John_Wells_(TV_producer)" class="mw-redirect" title="John Wells (TV producer)">John Wells</a> stated he believes that using the DGA agreement as a template, the strike could be easily resolved within two weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">[271]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">[272]</a></sup> Other writers disagreed with Wells' positive assessment.<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">[273]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Screen_Actors_Guild">Screen Actors Guild</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_Writers_Guild_of_America_strike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Screen Actors Guild">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Like the WGA, the <a href="/wiki/Screen_Actors_Guild" title="Screen Actors Guild">Screen Actors Guild</a> (SAG) is very concerned with residuals in new media and were especially supportive of the WGA's strike effort.<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">[274]</a></sup> SAG president <a href="/wiki/Alan_Rosenberg" title="Alan Rosenberg">Alan Rosenberg</a> suggested that SAG could choose to ignore the tradition of pattern bargaining if terms of the DGA's deal were deemed insufficient to the actors. Thus, if the new media issue was not resolved to their satisfaction by the DGA or WGA by July 2008, SAG was likely to strike when their contract expired, a move which could potentially bring the Hollywood film industry to a near-complete standstill.<sup id="cite_ref-strikezone_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-strikezone-77">[77]</a></sup> The previous deal between the SAG and AMPTP expired on June 30, 2008; however, on May 6 both organizations had without a deal ended talks.<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">[275]</a></sup> The SAG scheduled a rally for the morning of June 9 in Los Angeles; the WGA subsequently encouraged its members to support SAG members in that rally.<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">[276]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Outcomes">Outcomes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_Writers_Guild_of_America_strike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Outcomes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On November 19, 2008 the <a href="/wiki/Writers_Guild_of_America" title="Writers Guild of America">Writers Guild of America</a> announced they were filing <a href="/wiki/Arbitration" title="Arbitration">arbitration</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Alliance_of_Motion_Picture_%26_Television_Producers" class="mw-redirect" title="Alliance of Motion Picture &amp; Television Producers">Alliance of Motion Picture &amp; Television Producers</a> for not honoring the agreement that ended the strike.<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">[277]</a></sup> The matter was resolved with WGA and AMPTP, and a new agreement took effect on May 2, 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-Agreement_278-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Agreement-278">[278]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_Writers_Guild_of_America_strike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2007-12-19</span></span>. <q>The Horror Writers Association, on behalf of its writer members, stands in support of the Writers Guild of America strike in seeking appropriate compensation for writers when their work is distributed digitally, either via DVD or Internet downloads. All writers will be affected by the outcome of this strike, and we stand in solidarity, resisting those who seek to distribute our work on the Internet, DVD, or any format without fair compensation.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3A2007%9308+Writers+Guild+of+America+strike&amp;rft.atitle=Horror+Writers+Association&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fhorror.org%2F&amp;rft.jtitle=Horror+headlines&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>
